  1. I love this epilator. It was my first purchase into the world of epilating. It stings just a little for the first few times you use it and then after that - its not noticeable.   3. I read many reviews and mulled over this purchase before deciding to buy. I LOVE this epilator, and I've used 2 other oher brands. The great thing about this epilator is the \\"fingers\\" attachment. Which reduces pain considerably. Lower legs are easy, but I now use them on my armpits with much more ease than I thought! It's scarier in concept, than in actuality, the key is to have the hairs be about a centimeter long, at the most. I've also just recently started doing my bikini area (no, really) and it wasn't much worse than the armpits! I'm saving hundreds of dollars on waxes, and lots of annoying equipment, water, and razors by nothing having the shave. The only bad part is that it doesn't get all of the fine hairs on the upper leg, but it gets a good portion (70-80%) enough so that the upper leg is incredibly smooth.<br /><br />I do notice that I do have hairs growing under the skin, but this is true with ANY other epilator, and certainly with waxing.<br /><br />This product is fantastic and everything I thought it would be, and more. ESPECIALLY for the price. The charge hold for 1-3 weeks, depending on how often I use it. I can throw it into a bag for trips. It makes my life easy and saves me loads of money. I even got my mom one for Christmas, and she loves it!<br /><br />Most of the negative reviews are from people who thought that spinning rows of tweezers would be painless.
  4. This is my first epilator and I'm very happy with the Emjoi. I'm glad I opted for the cordless, as I can see how using a corded unit could be cumbersome. The size of the head is big enough to be efficient on large areas such as legs, but small enough to work in smaller areas like bikini.

The cord on the corded version is quite long and I've used it everywhere, even when traveling. There's always an outlet you can drag a chair next to.<br /><br />The reason for this recommendation is that when the cordless' battery dies, your otherwise-fully-functional Emjoi is toast. I'm not interested in replacing a $50-$60 item every couple of years. The corded ones last many times longer for this reason.<br /><br />(2) As at least one other reviewer has mentioned, you really need to use one hand to pull your skin taut. Not really on your legs, but definitely on your bikini area. While the epilator will stop turning if it pinches your skin (a safety feature), that doesn't make it hurt any less!<br /><br />(3) Having talked to several women who've used this, I've come to the conclusion that you can't predict whether you, personally, will find it too painful to use or not, so make sure you'll be able to return it if this is your first foray into epilator-land. For instance, I use it quite comfortably on my bikini area and legs, but just cannot tolerate it under my arms (most unfortunate!), while another woman I know has no problem using it on her legs and armpits but just can't use it on her bikini area.

And it's course thick Italian hair. And it grows quick, I could shave my legs in the morning and feel stubble at night. Ok, so, I had shaved a couple of days before and I start the Emjoi on my legs. It hurt much more! But, nothing I couldn't handle and certainly less than the laser hair treatments did. The problem was, it took forever! I had to go over and over the same area on my leg dozens of times. I even tried ignoring the instructions and going against hair growth, sideways across the growth, then I just hovered and did little circles. Even though I could handle the pain, after about an hour of it - it was starting to get to me. All in all, it took me over 2 hours to do my legs and they still weren't perfectly smooth, and the battery was dying, so I quit. Well, \\"Ok,\\" I thought, \\"That's probably because you have a lot of hair that wasn't long enough for the epilator to grab, we'll try again in a few days.\\" The good news is that it didn't take as long and hurt less, the bad news is that they weren't much smoother. I kept waiting for the hair to grow and trying again and again, but I just wasn't getting the results like I did with shaving. I finally cracked and shaved my legs a month and a half ago. Here's the crazy thing, now, when I use the epilator, they are significantly smoother. I have no real explanation other than that maybe it was dry skin I was feeling, not hair stubble, and the razor took care of it? So, I guess I can't blame the Emjoi for that.<br /><br />After a couple of weeks, I got enough guts to try it on my under arms. Mother of God - the pain. After a constant stream of explicits, I did have great success removing the hair! As with shaving, I found the hair grew in multiple directions so I had to change the direction I was running the tool to get all the hair. The good news is that the Emjoi did a great job removing the hair to the roots and I no longer had that underarm shadow. More good news, is that after a couple of touch-up treatments, I've found I only need to do it once a week or less. Yet even MORE good news, is that the pain is all by gone after using it for a couple of months. I had been thinking of getting laser treatments on my underarms. But now, I plan on saving a couple of hundred dollars and will just use this!<br /><br />I've been using it for about 3 months now and here's the breakdown for me with this hair removal tool:<br /><br />Forearms (with laser treatment):<br />Pain level - minimal<br />Removal Time - 15 min<br />Growback period - For any hair, a couple of weeks. However, its been 3 months and not enough has grown back to bother me so much I need to do it again<br /><br />Legs:<br />Pain level - Medium/Medium-high<br />Removal Time - First time: 2 hours, Subsequent times: 15-30 min<br />Growback period - 5-7 days<br /><br />Underarms:<br />Pain level - First time: Mother of God, Subsequent Times: Minimal<br />Removal Time - &lt; 5 min<br />Growback period - Just over a week<br /><br />Conclusion: This was my first epilator so I can't say if it works better or worse than others. Nor can I say if it hurts more or less. It got the job done and I think I'm going to be an epilator user for life now. However, I do find it takes a long time to do my legs. So, someday, I might look for a faster model, maybe one with more tweezers? The flip side is that I feel that more tweezers might hurt more... All in all, I'm glad I purchased this andI think it is a great first time epilator for people.
